فمنهم من قال إنه يمكن أن يكون البعض منها كان داخلا تحت بعض وذلك لأن الأجناس العالية من العشرة التي مرَّ ذكرها أربعة «الجوهر» والكمية» و«الكيفية» و«النسبة» ؛ إذ النسبة جنس للسبعة الباقية لكنه في حيز المنع . فإنها إذا كانت جنسًا لما تحتها كانت تلك النسبة وهي التي تحتها مركبة في ذاتها ؛ وذلك لا يمكن فإن النسبة متحققة بين الأجزاء. فتلك النسبة إن كانت مركبة كانت بين أجزائها نسبة أخرى، وإنه يفضي إلى المحال متناهية كانت تلك النسبة إلى البسائط من النسب أو لا متناهية. ومنهم من قال إنها أربعة «الجوهر» و «الكم» و«الكيف» و«المضاف»، وهذه في حيز المنع أيضًا لاستعماله على الفساد الذي مرَّ ذكره في ذلك. فمنهم من جعل الستة في جنس خامس إذا عد الأربعة، وللخامس الأطراف التي تأخذ من الكيفية شيئًا، وبطلان هذا المذهب وما هو بمثله لا يخفى عليك بعد الاطلاع على رسوم هذه العشرة وخواصها فيتضح لك أنها متباينة لا يمكن أن يكون البعض منها داخلا في البعض. وإن المضاف لا يكون شاملا للسبعة الباقية على الخصوص؛ إذ الحق في باب المضاف أن المضاف الحقيقي لا يحمل على شيء من المقولات حمل الجنس ولكن يوجد في كل واحد منها بأن يعرض له فيكون له نسبة إلى شيء يصير بها مضافا إليه من غير أن يصير المضاف جنساله. ولا يظن أن الشيء من حيث إن له شيئًا أو في شيء أو مع شيء مضاف بل بأن يأخذه بعدد ذلك من حيث له ذلك؛ فيعرض له أن تكون ماهيته بهذا الاعتبار مقولة بالقياس إلى غيره. فإنه كون زيد في الدار هو النسبة التي هو بها أين، وهذه النسبة ليست إضافة بل عينا. ثم باعتبار التكرر وحد الموقوف. فالأين يعرض له من حيث هو ذو أين أن يصير مقول الماهية بالقياس إلى ما هو فيه لا من حيث هو أين فقط؛ بل من حيث إنه محوي وذلك حاويه تعرض له الإضافة فليس كون الشيء في المكان الذي هو نسبة طرف واحد هو نفس كون ماهية مقولة بالقياس إلى غيره؛ بل موضوع، الكتب لكنه لا يلزم أن يكون كذلك. ولو كان كذلك فلفظة الأطراف لا تدل في هذا الموضع على معنى محصل، والأخذ من الكيفية شيئًا هو لفظ متشابه فلا يفهم منه ما يصلح أن يحكم عليه بكذا. ثم من المعلوم أن الشيء لا يكون متصفّا بصفة الجنسية إلا وأن يكون الغير الذي هو جنسه داخلا فيه بالذات، فإنه إذا كان داخلا فيه بالعرض فلا يكون هو جنسا، ولا يكون ذلك نوعا كذلك. ونَحنُ لا نجد من الأطراف ما يكون غيره داخلا فيه بالذات فلا يمكننا أن نحكم بجنسية تلك الأطراف. اللهم إلا أن يقال المعنى من الأطراف التي تأخذ من الكيفية شيئًا هو هذا الأمر، وحينئذ ننظر في ذلك الأمر أنه هل يصلح للجنسية أم لا؟ بل الحق أنه لا يصلح وإلا لا تكون الأجناس العالية عشرة.
Section: [That it is impossible for some of these ten to be subsumed under others]. And it is impossible for some of these ten to be subsumed under others, because if it were subsumed under another, it would be subsumed under a genus, and that is impossible for what has passed. Among them are those who said that it is possible for some of them to be subsumed under others, because the high genera of the ten that were mentioned are four: substance, quantity, quality, and relation; for relation is a genus for the remaining seven, but this is subject to denial. For if it were a genus for what is under it, then that relation (and what is under it) would be composite in itself; and that is impossible, because relation is realized between parts. So that relation, if it were composite, would have another relation between its parts, and that leads to an absurdity, whether that relation is finite to simple relations or infinite. And among them are those who said they are four: substance, quantity, quality, and relation, and these are also subject to denial because of the corruption that was mentioned earlier. Among them are those who made the six into a fifth genus when counting the four, and for the fifth the 'extremities' that take something from quality. The falsehood of this doctrine and what is like it is not hidden from you after examining the definitions and properties of these ten; it becomes clear that they are distinct and that it is impossible for some of them to be subsumed into others. And relation does not encompass the remaining seven specifically; for the truth in the topic of relation is that true relation is not predicated of any of the categories as a genus, but it exists in each of them as an accident, so that it has a relation to something by which it becomes relative, without relation becoming its genus. And one should not think that a thing insofar as it has something, or is in something, or is with something, is relative; rather, one takes it by the number of that insofar as it has that; then it accidentally happens that its quiddity in this respect is a category in relation to something else. For instance, 'Zayd being in the house' is the relation by which he is 'where' (ayna), and this relation is not relation (idafa) but rather the category of 'where' (ayna). Then, by considering repetition and the limit of the stopping point. So 'where' accidentally happens insofar as it is a 'where' that it becomes a quidditive category in relation to what it is in, not insofar as it is 'where' only; rather, insofar as it is contained and that is its container, relation accidentally happens to it. So the thing's being in place, which is a relation of one side, is not the same as the quiddity being a category in relation to something else; rather, it is a subject for that, insofar as the relation encompasses both sides of container and contained. This becomes clear to you in the topic of relation. As for their saying 'the extremities that take something from quantity', it resembles that by this is meant the categories of 'to act' (an yaf'ala) and 'to be acted upon' (an yanfa'ila) and 'position' (al-wad'); because quality is what leads to action and passion, and position also because it accompanies shape or shape accompanies it. And the extremities are the relation of the agent to the action, the relation of the patient to the passion, and the relation of position to shape, as is written in some books, but it is not necessary to be so. Even if it were so, the term 'extremities' in this context does not indicate a meaningful concept, and 'taking something from quality' is an ambiguous expression, so one cannot understand from it what can be judged by such. Then it is known that a thing is not described by the attribute of being a genus unless the other which is its genus is included in it essentially; for if it is included accidentally, then it is not a genus, nor is that a species accordingly. And we do not find among the extremities anything whose other is included in it essentially, so we cannot judge that those extremities are genera. Unless it is said that the meaning of 'extremities that take something from quality' is this matter; then we look into that matter to see whether it is suitable for being a genus or not. Rather, the truth is that it is not suitable, otherwise the high genera would not be ten.
Source pages p. 199

Commentary
This passage is a critical refutation of the view that some of the ten Aristotelian categories (al-maqulat al-'ashr) can be subsumed under others as species under a genus. The author establishes first the impossibility: if one category were under another, it would be under a genus, contradicting the fact that each category is a highest genus. Then he examines three erroneous opinions. First, some claim the high genera are only four: substance, quantity, quality, and relation, with relation being the genus for the other seven. The author denies this, arguing that relation is not composite in itself; if it were a genus, it would be composite, requiring further relations ad infinitum. Second, others propose four: substance, quantity, quality, and relation (with 'relation' as a distinct category), but this is similarly rejected due to the same corruption. Third, some attempt to make a fifth genus out of the remaining six (action, passion, position, when, where, and possession) by calling them 'extremities' (atraf) that take something from quality. The author refutes this by noting that true relation (al-mudaf) is not a genus but an accident in each category. He uses the example of 'Zayd being in the house' to show that the category of 'where' (ayna) is not relation (idafa) but a distinct category. He then critiques the term 'extremities', arguing it lacks clear meaning and does not satisfy the condition for genus-hood: a genus must be essentially included in its species. Since the purported 'extremities' do not have their other essentially included, they cannot be genera. The passage concludes that the ten categories remain distinct and irreducible.

Key Terms
المقولات العشر
النسبة
المضاف
الأطراف
الجنس

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author, what is the fatal flaw in making 'relation' a genus for the other seven categories?
A) Relation is a substance, not a genus.
B) Relation would then be composite, leading to infinite regress.
C) Relation is only found in the category of 'when'.
D) The other categories are not species of relation.

Key Takeaway
A highest genus cannot be subsumed under another because subsumption requires essential inclusion, and for categories like relation, such inclusion leads to absurd composition.

Refuting the Claim that 'Extremities' are Genera
Author refutes the claim that 'extremities' are genera

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate whether a given term qualifies as a genus by applying the essential inclusion condition.

Core Idea
A genuine genus must have its species essentially included, not accidentally.

This passage refutes an attempt to treat certain abstract concepts—called 'extremities' of quantity—as genera. The author argues that the term is ambiguous and fails the fundamental condition for genus-dom: the species must be essentially included in the genus. Understanding this refutation sharpens your ability to test categorical distinctions in Islamic logic.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Claim
The claim is that 'extremities' (al-atraf) taken from quantity are the categories of action, passion, and position. Find the terms in the Arabic and understand what is being asserted.
The claim is quoted from 'some books'.
2
Detect the Ambiguity
The author says the term 'extremities' does not have a determinate meaning, and 'taking something from quality' is ambiguous. Notice how the author dismisses the claim on grounds of vagueness before applying logical criteria.
This is a preliminary objection: the claim's terms are not clear enough to judge.
3
State the Genus Condition
The author states that for X to be a genus, the species must be essentially (bi al-dhat) included in X, not accidentally. Extract this condition from the text.
Essential inclusion means the genus is part of the essence of the species.
4
Test the Extremities
Examine whether any 'extremity' has something else essentially included in it. The author says we do not find such a relation. Therefore, they cannot be genera.
The test fails because the alleged species are not essentially included in the extremities.
5
Consider the Consequence
If the extremities were accepted as genera, the number of highest genera would exceed ten, contradicting the established doctrine that there are ten categories.
This is a reductio ad absurdum: the claim leads to an untenable result.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما قولهم إن الأطراف التي تأخذ من الكمية شيئاً يشبه أن يكون المعنى بهذا مقولة أن يفعل وأن ينفعل والوضع؛ إذ الكيفية هي التي تسوق إليه الفعل والانفعال، والوضع أيضًا لما أنه يلزم الشكل أو يلزمه الشكل. والأطراف هي نسبة الفاعل إلى الفعل ونسبة المنفعل إلى الانفعال ونسبة الوضع إلى الشكل كما هو المسطور في البعض من الكتب لكنه لا يلزم أن يكون كذلك. ولو كان كذلك فلفظة الأطراف لا تدل في هذا الموضع على معنى محصل، والأخذ من الكيفية شيئًا هو لفظ متشابه فلا يفهم منه ما يصلح أن يحكم عليه بكذا. ثم من المعلوم أن الشيء لا يكون متصفًّا بصفة الجنسية إلا وأن يكون الغير الذي هو جنسه داخلًا فيه بالذات، فإنه إذا كان داخلًا فيه بالعرض فلا يكون هو جنسًا، ولا يكون ذلك نوعًا كذلك. ونحن لا نجد من الأطراف ما يكون غيره داخلًا فيه بالذات فلا يمكننا أن نحكم بجنسية تلك الأطراف. اللهم إلا أن يقال المعنى من الأطراف التي تأخذ من الكيفية شيئًا هو هذا الأمر، وحينئذ ننظر في ذلك الأمر أنه هل يصلح للجنسية أم لا؟ بل الحق أنه لا يصلح وإلا لا تكون الأجناس العالية عشرة.
And as for their statement that 'the extremities which take something from quantity,' it resembles that the meaning by this is the category of action, passion, and position; for quality is what leads to action and passion, and position also because it necessitates shape or shape necessitates it. And the extremities are the relation of the agent to the action, the relation of the patient to the passion, and the relation of position to the shape, as is recorded in some books, but it is not necessarily so. And if it were so, then the term 'extremities' does not indicate in this place a determinate meaning, and 'taking something from quality' is an ambiguous expression, so it cannot be understood from it what is suitable to be judged upon. Then it is known that a thing cannot be characterized by the attribute of genus unless the other which is its genus is essentially included in it; if it is accidentally included, then it is not a genus, nor is that a species. And we do not find among the extremities anything whose other is essentially included in it, so we cannot judge that those extremities are genera. Unless it is said that the meaning of 'the extremities which take something from quality' is this matter, and then we look into that matter whether it is suitable for genus-dom or not. Rather, the truth is that it is not suitable, otherwise the highest genera would not be ten.
Source pages p. 200

Commentary
This passage is a critical refutation of a claim that the 'extremities' (الأطراف) taken from quantity can be considered as the categories of action, passion, and position. The author begins by noting that the claim is ambiguous: the term 'extremities' is not clearly defined, and 'taking something from quality' is vague. He then applies a logical principle: for something to be a genus, the lower species must be essentially included in it, not accidentally. The author argues that among these 'extremities', there is no instance where another thing is essentially included in them, so they cannot serve as genera. He concludes that if they were genera, the number of highest genera would exceed ten, which contradicts the agreed-upon doctrine that they are ten. The argument uses the internal logic of the genus-species relationship, common in Islamic logic for validating categorical distinctions.

The condition for genus-dom is essential inclusion; ambiguous or accidental relations do not create valid genera.

The Ten Categories

7 min
The Division of the Ten Categories
Author presents the standard division of the ten categories.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to trace the hierarchical division of the ten categories, identifying substance, accident, and the subdivisions of accident.

Core Idea
The ten categories are derived from a binary division: substance vs. accident, then accident by division and relation.

In Islamic logic, the ten categories (al-maqūlāt al-ʿashr) provide a comprehensive classification of all existents. This classification is not merely philosophical; it underpins definitions in kalām, uṣūl al-fiqh, and other sciences. Understanding how the categories are derived from a few binary distinctions will sharpen your ability to analyze any concept.

Guided Path
1
Identify the root division
Note the first split: that which is either subsistent in itself (substance) or subsistent in another (accident). This is the fundamental cleavage.
Substance (jawhar) does not need a subject; accident (ʿaraḍ) does.
2
Examine the first subdivision of accident
Accidents are divided based on two criteria: whether the accident yields division (quantity) and whether it yields relation. Quantity yields division; quality does not yield relation.
Reference the passage: 'accident is not free from either yielding from its truth the truth of division, which is quantity, or not yielding.'
3
Examine the subdivision of relation
Relation (nisba) is further divided into repeated relation (idāfa) and non-repeated relation. Non-repeated relation includes place (ayn), time (matā), posture (jidda), position (waḍʿ), action (an yafʿala), and passion (an yanfaʿila).
These seven complete the list of categories.
4
Construct the full tree
Draw the hierarchy: substance (1) + accident → if yields division: quantity (2); if not, then if not yields relation: quality (3); if yields relation: if repeated: relation/idāfa (4); if not: place (5), time (6), posture (7), position (8), action (9), passion (10).
Memorize the ten: jawhar, kammiyya, kayfiyya, idāfa, ayn, matā, jidda, waḍʿ, an yafʿala, an yanfaʿila.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والمفهوم عند الجمهور أنها عشرة؛ إذ الذي يكون منها إما أن يكون قائمًا بذاته وهو الجوهر، أو لا يكون قائمًا بذاته بل بالغير وهو العرض. والعرض لا يخلو من أن يحصل من صدقه صدق القسمة وهو الكمية، أو لا يحصل. وإنه لا يخلو من أن لا يحصل من صدقه صدق النسبة وهو الكيفية، أو يحصل وهو النسبة. والنسبة إما أن تكون مكررة وهي الإضافة أو لا تكون. وإنها إما من جهة المكان وهي الأين، أو الزمان وهي المتى، أو الإحاطة وهي الجدة، أو الهيئة الحاصلة للجسم وهي الوضع، أو الفاعلية وهي أن يفعل، أو القابلية وهي أن ينفعل. وأما قول من قال إن الانفعال هو الكيفية ليس إلا؛ إذ التسخن ليس غير السخونة بل هو عينها، فذلك باطل؛ إذ التسخن وهو السلوك إلى السخونة بهيئة غير قارة والسخونة هيئة قارة. وكذلك قول من يقول إن الحركة جنس لأن يفعل وأن ينفعل؛ إذ هو باطل أيضًا لما أن الحركة غير موصوف بها الفاعل وإنها ليست تفعل أيضًا على ما عرف في العلم الطبيعي.
And the understanding among the majority is that they are ten; for that which is among them is either subsistent in itself, which is substance, or not subsistent in itself but by another, which is accident. And accident is not free from either yielding from its truth the truth of division, which is quantity, or not yielding. And it is not free from either not yielding from its truth the truth of relation, which is quality, or yielding, which is relation. And relation is either repeated, which is relation (idafa), or not. And it is either from the aspect of place, which is where (ayn), or time, which is when (mata), or encompassing, which is posture (jidda), or the form obtained for the body, which is position (wad'), or agentivity, which is to act (an yaf'ala), or receptivity, which is to be acted upon (an yanfa'ila). As for the statement of one who said that passion is nothing but quality, for heating is nothing other than heat but is identical to it, that is false; for heating is the striving toward heat with a non-stable state, while heat is a stable state. And similarly the statement of one who says that motion is a genus for action and passion; that is also false because motion is not attributed to the agent and it is not an action either, as is known in natural science.
Source pages p. 201

Commentary
This passage is a definitional exposition of the ten Aristotelian categories as understood by the majority of logicians. The author begins by dividing existents into substance (جوهر), which subsists by itself, and accident (عرض), which subsists through another. Accident is then further divided based on two criteria: whether it entails division (quantity) and whether it entails relation. If an accident does not entail division, it may either not entail relation (quality) or entail relation (relation/nisba). Relation is subdivided into repeated relation (idafa) and non-repeated, which includes place (ayn), time (mata), posture (jidda), position (wad'), action (an yaf'ala), and passion (an yanfa'ila). The author then refutes two objections: first, someone claimed that passion (infi'al) is nothing but quality (kayfiyya), but the author argues that heating (example of passion) is a process toward heat, not the stable state of heat itself. Second, someone claimed that motion is a genus for action and passion, but the author rejects this because motion is not attributed to the agent as an action, as established in natural science. This passage provides a clear classification of the ten categories and defends the standard divisions.

Key Takeaway
The ten categories are derived from a binary tree rooted in the distinction between substance and accident, with accidents further classified by division and relation.

Refuting Two Objections to the Categories
Author refutes two objections against the standard categories.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to refute the misconception that passion is identical to quality and that motion is a genus for action and passion, using distinctions from the passage.

Core Idea
Passion is a process (non-stable), not a stable quality; motion is not attributable to the agent as an action.

The author defends the standard list of categories against two specific objections. Understanding these refutations deepens your grasp of the categories, especially the subtle difference between quality and passion, and between action and motion. These distinctions are crucial in kalām debates about the nature of accidents.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first objection
The first objection claims that passion (infiʿāl) is nothing but quality (kayfiyya), using the example of heating: heating is the same as heat.
The opponent says: 'التسخن ليس غير السخونة بل هو عينها'.
2
Analyze the author's refutation
The author distinguishes between heating (a process, a non-stable state) and heat (a stable quality). Passion is the process, not the stable state, so it cannot be reduced to quality.
Heating is 'السلوك إلى السخونة بهيئة غير قارة' while heat is 'هيئة قارة'.
3
Identify the second objection
The second objection claims that motion (ḥaraka) is a genus for action and passion, meaning action and passion fall under motion.
The opponent says: 'الحركة جنس لأن يفعل وأن ينفعل'.
4
Analyze the author's refutation
The author rejects this based on natural science: motion is not attributed to the agent as an action (i.e., the agent does not 'move' in the same sense), and motion itself is not an action.
The passage says: 'الحركة غير موصوف بها الفاعل وإنها ليست تفعل أيضًا'.

Entities Beyond the Ten Categories
Author lists examples of mental entities that do not fall under the ten categories.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and classify examples of mental entities that do not fall under Aristotle's ten categories.

Core Idea
Not all that exists in the mind fits into the ten categories – some are principles, privations, or underlying substrata.

In this passage, the author lists several examples of things that exist in the imagination but are not included in the ten categories of substance and accident. These include unity, the point, matter, form, and privations like blindness. Understanding these helps clarify the scope of the categories and prevents confusion in logical classification.

Guided Path
1
Identify the topic
The author introduces things that are 'disparate from these ten' – what does 'disparate' mean? Why are they not categories?
Disparate means separate or outside; these entities exist in the mind but do not fit the categorical framework.
2
List the examples given
Find the Arabic terms for unity, point, matter, form, and privations (blindness, ignorance).
Write them down: الوحدة, النقطة, الهيولى, الصورة, الأعدام.
3
Understand each example's nature
Why is unity not a category? Because it is a principle of number, not a quantity itself. Why is the point not a magnitude? It is the principle of measurement. Matter and form are hylomorphic components. Privations are absences of a positive attribute.
Each example is either a principle or a privation, not an independent category.
4
Analyze the author's caution
The author warns that not every existence is outside categories; some specific examples (north/south, morning/evening) are incorrectly adduced. They are actually categories (e.g., relative position, time).
The caution ensures we do not overextend the list; categories remain ten.
5
Apply the concept
Think of another entity that might be mistakenly thought to be a category but is not, e.g., 'existence' itself. Why is it not a category?
Existence is a universal concept, not a category; categories are types of existents.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل: في ما يكون في الأوهام من الأمور المباينة لهذه العشرة. وما يكون في الأوهام من الأمور المباينة لهذه العشرة، فذلك كالوحدة التي هي مبدأ العدد والنقطة التي هي مبدأ بوجه ما للمقادير، وأيضًا مثل الهيولى والصورة، وأيضًا مثل الأعدام كالعمى والجهل وما أشبه ذلك. فمنهم من أورد في هذا الباب أمثلة جزئية، نحو الشمال والجنوب والغداء والعشاء؛ فنقول إنه ليس كل وجود الأشياء لا يدخل في المقولات. رمز (١) في أن المقولات عشرة، وليس يجب في بادي الرأي أن يكون لكل ذات موجودة ما يشاركه في الذات.
A chapter: On what exists in the imaginations among things that are disparate from these ten. And what exists in the imaginations among things that are disparate from these ten, that is like unity which is the principle of number, and the point which is in a way the principle of magnitudes, and also like matter and form, and also like privations such as blindness and ignorance and the like. So some have adduced in this chapter particular examples, such as north and south and morning and evening; we say that not every existence of things does not enter into the categories. A symbol that the categories are ten, and it is not necessary at first view that every existent essence has something that shares in the essence.
Source pages p. 201

Commentary
This passage is a classification of things that exist in the mind (awham) but fall outside the ten categories. The author begins by stating the topic: things in the imagination that are disparate from the ten categories. He then gives examples: unity (الوحدة) as the principle of number, the point (النقطة) as the principle of magnitudes, matter (الهيولى) and form (الصورة) from hylomorphism, and privations (الأعدام) like blindness and ignorance. He notes that some have given particular examples like north/south and morning/evening, then cautions that not every existence of things is excluded from the categories. The marginal note reminds that the categories are ten, and it is not necessary that every existent essence shares in the essence of a category. This passage clarifies that certain conceptual entities, though mentally existing, are not categories themselves but principles or privations.

D) Because it is a substance.

Key Takeaway
Mental entities like unity, point, matter, form, and privations exist in the imagination but are not among the ten categories; they are principles or absences, not categorical existences.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Identify which of the following is NOT a category: unity, point, matter, form, blindness. Explain why each is not a category using the author's reasoning.
?
The author says that 'not every existence of things does not enter into the categories'. Provide an example of a mental concept that does fall under the categories (e.g., knowledge as a quality, or whiteness as an accident) and explain why it fits.

The Ten Categories
intermediate
10 min
The Ten Categories: Classification by Self-Subsistence and Relation
Author defines the ten categories via a divisional tree.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify any existent into one of the ten categories by tracing the division tree from substance to accident to the subtypes of relation.

Core Idea
The ten categories partition all existents based on self-subsistence and type of relation.

The ten categories (al-maqūlāt al-ʿashr) are the fundamental genera into which all existents fall. The author begins with the broadest division—self-subsistent versus non-self-subsistent—and then subdivides accidents based on whether they entail division, relation, and further specifications. This lesson walks you through that divisional tree so you can place any entity in its proper category.

Guided Path
1
Identify the primary division
Start by determining whether the existent is self-subsistent (standing on its own) or depends on another. The first is substance (jawhar), the second is accident (ʿaraḍ).
Substance is defined as 'qāʾim bi-dhātihi'.
2
Distinguish accidents by division and relation
If it is an accident, check whether its truth (ṣidq) entails divisibility into parts. If yes, it is quantity (kammiyya). If not, check whether its truth entails a relation (nisba). If relation is absent, it is quality (kayfiyya). If relation is present, it falls under relation.
Relation here is a general category including specific relations.
3
Subdivide relation into repeated or not
If the relation is 'repeated' (mukarrara)—i.e., reciprocal—it is iḍāfa (relation in the specific sense, e.g., fatherhood). If not repeated, move to the next step.
Iḍāfa involves two relata, like paternity/filiation.
4
Identify the seven remaining categories
The non-repeated relations are specified by the aspect of the relation: place (ayn), time (matā), envelopment (jidda, possession), disposition of parts (waḍʿ, position), agency (an yafʿal, action), or passivity (an yanfaʿil, passion).
These seven, together with substance, quantity, quality, and iḍāfa, make ten.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والمفهوم عند الجمهور أنها عشرة؛ إذ الذي يكون منها إما أن يكون قائما بذاته وهو الجوهر، أو لا يكون قائما بذاته بل بالغير وهو العرض والعرض لا يخلو من أن يحصل من صدقه صدق القسمة وهو الكمية، أو لا يحصل، وإنه لا يخلو من أن لا يحصل من صدقه صدق النسبة وهو الكيفية، أو يحصل وهو النسبة. والنسبة إما أن تكون مكررة وهي الإضافة أو لا تكون. وإنها إما من جهة المكان وهي الأين، أو الزمان وهي المتى، أو الإحاطة وهي الجُدة، أو الهيئة الحاصلة للجسم وهي الوضع أو الفاعلية وهي أن يفعل، أو القابلية وهي أن ينفعل. وأما قول من قال إن الانفعال هو الكيفية ليس إلا؛ إذ التسخن ليس غير السخونة بل هو عينها» فذلك باطل؛ إذ التسخن وهو السلوك إلى السخونة بهيئة غير قارة والسخونة هيئة قارة. وكذلك قول من يقول إن الحركة جنس لأن يفعل وأن ينفعل»؛ إذ هو باطل أيضًا لما أن الحركة غير موصوف بها الفاعل وإنها ليست تفعل أيضًا على ما عرف في العلم الطبيعي.
And the concept according to the majority is that they are ten; because that which exists is either self-subsistent and that is substance, or not self-subsistent but by another and that is accident. And accident is not free from either that from its truth the truth of division obtains and that is quantity, or it does not obtain. And it is not free from either that from its truth the truth of relation does not obtain and that is quality, or it obtains and that is relation. And relation is either repeated and that is relation (addition), or not. And it is either with respect to place and that is 'ayn, or time and that is matā, or surrounding and that is possession, or the disposition acquired for the body and that is position, or agency and that is to do, or passivity and that is to be acted upon. As for the statement of one who said that passion is nothing but quality, because heating is nothing other than heat but is it itself, that is false; because heating is the progression towards heat in a non-stable state and heat is a stable state. And similarly the statement of one who says that motion is a genus of to do and to be acted upon is also false, because motion is not attributed to the agent and it is not an action either, as is known in natural science.
Source pages p. 201

Commentary
This passage defines the ten categories (maqūlāt) as understood by the majority. The author begins by dividing all existents into substance (jawhar) and accident (ʿaraḍ). Accidents are then subdivided: some involve division into parts (quantity: kammiyya), some involve relation (nisba): if relation is not obtained, it is quality; if obtained, it is relation. Relation is further differentiated: if repeated, it is iḍāfa (relation in the specific sense); otherwise, it is place (ayn), time (matā), possession (jidda), position (waḍʿ), action (an yafʿal), or passion (an yanfaʿil). The author then refutes two objections: (1) that passion is merely quality, arguing that heating (tasakhkhun) is a process leading to heat (sukhūna), which is a stable state, so they are distinct; (2) that motion is a genus encompassing action and passion, but motion is not attributable to an agent as an action, as established in natural science.

الكيفية

الجدة

أن ينفعل

Checkpoint
According to the text, which of the following is a necessary condition for something to be an accident?
A) It must be self-subsistent.
B) It must exist through another (bil-ghayr).
C) It must involve division into parts.
D) It must be a quality.

Key Takeaway
The ten categories are derived by a systematic division of existents into substance and accident, and further by properties of division and relation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Classify the following entities into the ten categories: a) a human body, b) the color black, c) the year 2024, d) the relationship of fatherhood, e) the action of writing, f) the state of being heated. For each, state which category it belongs to and explain your reasoning using the division tree.
?
Write a short paragraph explaining why 'time' is considered a separate category from 'place' in this scheme, based on the text's definition of 'matā' as relation with respect to time.
